<username>patrick kelly<//username>< Review>
It is amazing having a family owned business here in the community that cares about quality of service. We had a terrible water volume and discoloration problem.  The Huff's came out to troubleshoot and what was amazing, at no charge. Now that is customer service.

Brett noticed our system wasn't regenerating and got it working, with recommendations to frequently regenerate the system to unclog the system of the debris that had accumulated. Simply put this saved us from having to re-bed or buy a new unit.

He also suggested being on a well in our location, with so much Iron and manganese in the water, that we should have an Iron filter in front of our system. Which we invested in.  Bret re-piped everything from the main inlet pipe forward.  Very professionally done.  You can tell he takes extreme care to take the time and do the job right. They take great pride in their work and it is evident in the results, our water volume is up and the coloration is clear.

We would recommend Hague and the Huff's to anyone wanting to improve their water quality situation.<//Review>

<GmapID>0x80c2c78251984b6d:0x9b9c5efe2358cc08</GmapID><Time>1452785382479< /Time><UserId.>110873789351399723897</UserId.><Response>None<//Response><pictures>None</pictures>< review>
I was there to treat my non-Korean business partner a Korean course meal. I have to admit I never like the idea of a course meal so maybe I am biased.

At first, I thought the price was outrageous but reluctantly rationalized it as a course meal. However, the whole dining experience there really did not change my initial impression.
The dishes did not appear to be authentic or traditional to me and tasted rather bland to me except for the fish (a replacement of pork but was rather salty). The service was not impressive either. All they did was bringing out the dishes and they never paid attention to the needs of the customers. I had to walk up to the front to ask for an extra pair of chopsticks and forks to bone the fish and the change of the plates. I may be one of those impatient ones but the server was hardly around our table except for the time she brought out the dishes. In a way, it may be an inherent problem of this 'course meal' because the servers are busy bringing out the dishes. It was supposed to be a business lunch but I really could not focus on the conversation.

I truly regretted that I took her there and do not think I will ever go to one of these places on my own, especially if I have to pay. I hope the management of the restaurant reads this so that they could think about how to improve customers' dining experience.</review>

<pics>None</pics><resp>None< /resp><gmapID>0x80c2c78251984b6d:0x9b9c5efe2358cc08<//gmapID></record>

<Text>I guess this is the place for traditional Korean family gatherings. Came here to celebrate grandma's 90th bday. My uncle had reserved one of the private rooms on the first floor, which comfortably accommodated the 40 some-odd well-wishers. They had the buffet set up against the wall, and there was a projector screen and podium, as well as a large table of honor at the front of the room for grandma and grandpa (see photo).

The food was pretty good, tasted very homey. I ate most everything but skipped the kalbi jjim (braised short ribs) and the tang soo yuk (like a sweet and sour pork)--they didn't look that appetizing to me. I liked the the fried fish cakes, dumplings, and the various side dishes. The miso-based soup was pretty good, but it was weird to eat that out of styrofoam cups and a plastic spoon. Were they really out of proper dishes and utensils? There were regular plates and utensils for the other stuff, though. The best part was watching the white hubby eat the so-called "desserts"--an especially unsweet assortment of rice cakes that all the old people like. One kind was so unsweet it was akin to eating an eraser coated with bean powder. Yeah, he was kind of sad. :D Service was pretty decent, with a waitress devoted to our room fetching us water pitchers, distributing the cakes, etc. All in all an OK experience. I doubt I'd come back here just for the food--there are plenty of places closer to me that are just as good, but if you ever get invited to some Korean family gathering here at least you'll know the food will be decent.<//Text><response>None<//response><Rate>3<//Rate>< name>
Stephanie Han</name>

< review>
I love their lunch specials. Recently had the shrimp and asparagus with black bean sauce for 9.50. Included brown rice and salad. The honey dressing was a little sweet, but other than that small gripe, the lettuce was fresh, the shrimp was cooked perfect(not over cooked like many restaurants), the bean sauce was savery(not over sweetened like many Asian American restaurants) and the asparagus was perfect. Many lunch specials aren't very special but this one is. The wait staff was quick, and the atmosphere was modern. A solid dining experience.</review>

1513650042742< /Time>
< Rate>
4< /Rate>
< text>
Don't let the look of place fool you. The workers are slow to acknowledged you, but they know you're there. Festive colorful interior with standard set up and palm tree mirror. Looks dated, but totally functional place. Drop a dollar into wall mounted juke box and let the music play while you wait for your order. I got two steak tacos that's loaded with hot off the grill steak. They don't skimp on meat here. Normally I like tacos that holds well with no meat pieces falling out. In this case, it fell out and I had to finished the rest with a with a fork. But, that's okay though. A good find in the excelsior if your craving Mexican. Can't go wrong and certainly no harm to try. Enjoy! Btw, Dosa is not done yet wait till spring of next year hehehe.< /text>
